style="font-weight:normal;">(3)</span></th><td>\n<div class="hlist hlist-separated"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/2001_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2001 St. Louis Cardinals season">2001</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">2011</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/2012_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2012 St. Louis Cardinals season">2012</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #dcdcdc">Front office</th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Owner(s)</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/William_DeWitt_Jr." title="William DeWitt Jr.">William DeWitt Jr.</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Mike_Shildt" title="Mike Shildt">Mike Shildt</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">General Manager</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Michael_Girsch" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Girsch">Michael Girsch</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">President of Baseball Operations</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/John_Mozeliak" title="John Mozeliak">John Mozeliak</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>St. Louis Cardinals</b> are an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis" title="St. Louis">St. Louis, Missouri</a>. The Cardinals compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">Central</a> division. <a href="/wiki/Busch_Stadium" title="Busch Stadium">Busch Stadium</a> has been their home <a href="/wiki/Baseball_park" title="Baseball park">ballpark</a> since 2006. One of the most successful franchises in baseball history, the Cardinals have won 11 <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">World Series championships</a>, the second-most in Major League Baseball (behind the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>) and the most in the National League. Their 19 <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_pennant_winners" title="List of National League pennant winners">National League pennants</a> rank third in NL history. In addition, St. Louis has won 13 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_division_winners" title="Major League Baseball division winners">division titles</a> in the East and Central divisions.\n</p><p>While still in the old <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> (AA), named then as the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns_(NL)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns (NL)">St. Louis Browns</a>, the team won four AA league championships, qualifying them to play in the professional baseball championship tournament  (a <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-World_Series_baseball_champions" title="List of pre-World Series baseball champions">forerunner</a> of the modern  <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>, established 1903) of that era. They tied in <a href="/wiki/1885_World_Series" title="1885 World Series">1885</a> and won outright in <a href="/wiki/1886_World_Series" title="1886 World Series">1886</a> and lost in <a href="/wiki/1888_World_Series" title="1888 World Series">1888</a> for the early trophy <a href="/wiki/Hall_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Hall Cup">Hall Cup</a> versus the New York Giants.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The others both times against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a> (originally the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Stockings" title="Chicago White Stockings">Chicago White Stockings</a> then), in the first meetings of the <a href="/wiki/Cardinals%E2%80%93Cubs_rivalry" title="Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry">Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry</a> between nearby cities of <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago</a> that continues to this day.\n</p><p>With origins as one of the early professional baseball clubs in St. Louis and the nation, entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Chris_von_der_Ahe" title="Chris von der Ahe">Chris von der Ahe</a> purchased a <a href="/wiki/Barnstorm_(sports)" title="Barnstorm (sports)">barnstorming</a> club in 1881, then known as the <b>Brown Stockings</b>, and established them as charter members of the old <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> (AA) base ball league which played 1882 to 1891, the following season. Upon the discontinuation of the AA, St. Louis joined the continuing <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League of Professional Base Ball Clubs</a>, later known simply as the National League, (organized in 1876), in 1892; at that time, they were called the <b>Browns</b> (not to be confused with a later team also known as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Browns" title="History of the St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a>, 1902-1953) and also as the <b>Perfectos</b> before they were officially renamed eight years later as the <b>Cardinals</b> in 1900. The name refers to the bird called "Cardinal", which is the team\'s mascot, rather than to the senior Catholic Church officials so named.\n</p><p>Cardinals achievements that have impacted MLB and sports events in general include manager/owner <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a>\'s pioneering of the <a href="/wiki/Farm_team" title="Farm team">farm system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a>\'s two batting <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crowns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Dean" title="Dizzy Dean">Dizzy Dean</a>\'s 30-<a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)" title="Win\xe2\x80\x93loss record (pitching)">win</a> season in <a href="/wiki/1934_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1934 Major League Baseball season">1934</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a>\'s 17 MLB and 29 NL records, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>\'s 1.12 <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">earned run average</a> (ERA) in <a href="/wiki/1968_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1968 Major League Baseball season">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitey_Herzog" title="Whitey Herzog">Whitey Herzog</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Whiteyball" title="Whiteyball">Whiteyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGwire" title="Mark McGwire">Mark McGwire</a> breaking the <a href="/wiki/1998_Major_League_Baseball_home_run_record_chase" title="1998 Major League Baseball home run record chase">single-season home run record in 1998</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">2011 championship team\'s</a> unprecedented comebacks.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The Cardinals have won 105 or more games in four different seasons and won 100 or more a total of nine times. Cardinals players have won 20 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">league MVPs</a>, four batting Triple Crowns, and three <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a>. <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> inductees include <a href="/wiki/Lou_Brock" title="Lou Brock">Lou Brock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Dean" title="Dizzy Dean">Dizzy Dean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whitey_Herzog" title="Whitey Herzog">Whitey Herzog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Medwick" title="Joe Medwick">Joe Medwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_Schoendienst" title="Red Schoendienst">Red Schoendienst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Smith" title="Ozzie Smith">Ozzie Smith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Sutter" title="Bruce Sutter">Bruce Sutter</a>.\n</p><p>In 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> valued the Cardinals at $1.9 billion, making them the 7th-most valuable franchise in MLB; their revenue the previous year was $319 million, and their <a href="/wiki/Earnings_before_interest_and_taxes" title="Earnings before interest and taxes">operating income</a> was $40.0 million.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes2018_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2018-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes2016_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2016-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2015_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2015-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Since their purchase in 1995, <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_owners_and_executives" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals owners and executives">owner</a> <a href="/wiki/William_DeWitt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William DeWitt, Jr.">William DeWitt, Jr.</a>\'s investment group has seen enormous growth from the $147 million purchase price. <a href="/wiki/John_Mozeliak" title="John Mozeliak">John Mozeliak</a> is the President of Baseball Operations, Mike Girsch is the <a href="/wiki/General_manager_(baseball)" title="General manager (baseball)">general manager</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shildt" title="Mike Shildt">Mike Shildt</a> is the interim <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_managers" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals managers">manager</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frontoffice_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontoffice-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Cardinals are renowned for their strong fan support: despite being in one of the sport\'s mid-level markets, they routinely see attendances among the league\'s highest, and are consistently among the Top 3 in MLB in local television ratings.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_fans_best_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_fans_best-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ratings_among_highest_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratings_among_highest-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toclimit-3"><div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_seasons" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals seasons">List of St. Louis Cardinals seasons</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Cardinals_(1875%E2%80%931919)" title="History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1875\xe2\x80\x931919)">History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1875\xe2\x80\x931919)</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Before_the_Cardinals_.281875.E2.80.931881.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_the_Cardinals_(1875\xe2\x80\x931881)">Before the Cardinals (1875\xe2\x80\x931881)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Before the Cardinals (1875\xe2\x80\x931881)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Professional baseball began in St. Louis with the inception of the <b><a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Brown_Stockings" title="St. Louis Brown Stockings">Brown Stockings</a></b> in the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Professional_Base_Ball_Players" title="National Association of Professional Base Ball Players">National Association</a> (NA) <a href="/wiki/1875_St._Louis_Brown_Stockings_season" title="1875 St. Louis Brown Stockings season">in 1875</a>. The NA folded following that season, and <a href="/wiki/1876_St._Louis_Brown_Stockings_season" title="1876 St. Louis Brown Stockings season">the next season</a>, St. Louis joined the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> as a charter member, finishing in third place at 45-19. <a href="/wiki/George_Bradley" title="George Bradley">George Bradley</a> hurled the first <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a> in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_no-hitters" title="List of Major League Baseball no-hitters">Major League history</a>. The NL expelled St. Louis from the league <a href="/wiki/1877_St._Louis_Brown_Stockings_season" title="1877 St. Louis Brown Stockings season">after 1877</a> due to a game-fixing scandal and the team went bankrupt.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  Without a league, they continued play as a semi-professional <a href="/wiki/Barnstorm_(sports)" title="Barnstorm (sports)">barnstorming</a> team through 1881.\n</p><p>The magnitudes of the reorganizations following the 1877 and 1881 seasons are such that the 1875\xe2\x80\x931877 and 1878\xe2\x80\x931881 Brown Stockings teams are not generally considered to share continuity as a franchise with the current St. Louis Cardinals.<sup id="cite_ref-BR_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RS_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="American_Association_and_early_National_League_eras_.281882.E2.80.931919.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Association_and_early_National_League_eras_(1882\xe2\x80\x931919)">American Association and early National League eras (1882\xe2\x80\x931919)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: American Association and early National League eras (1882\xe2\x80\x931919)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg/220px-Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg/330px-Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg/440px-Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_Comiskey_circa_1910.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_Comiskey" title="Charles Comiskey">Charles Comiskey</a>, shown here circa 1910, guided the Browns to four <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> titles.</div></div></div>\n<p>For the <a href="/wiki/1882_St._Louis_Brown_Stockings_season" title="1882 St. Louis Brown Stockings season">1882 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_von_der_Ahe" title="Chris von der Ahe">Chris von der Ahe</a> purchased the team, reorganized it, and made it a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> (AA), a league to rival the NL.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> 1882 is generally considered to be the first year existence of the St. Louis Cardinals.<sup id="cite_ref-BR_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RS_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/1883_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1883 St. Louis Browns season">The next season</a>, St. Louis shortened their name to the <b>Browns</b>. Soon thereafter they became the dominant team in the AA, as manager <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Comiskey" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlie Comiskey">Charlie Comiskey</a> guided St. Louis to four pennants in a row from <a href="/wiki/1885_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1885 St. Louis Browns season">1885</a> to <a href="/wiki/1888_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1888 St. Louis Browns season">1888</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Comiskey_managerial_record_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Comiskey_managerial_record-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">Pitcher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outfielder" title="Outfielder">outfielder</a> <a href="/wiki/Bob_Caruthers" title="Bob Caruthers">Bob Caruthers</a> led the league in <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">ERA</a> (2.07) and <a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)" title="Win\xe2\x80\x93loss record (pitching)">wins</a> (40) in 1885 and finished in the top six in both in each of the following two seasons.  He also led the AA in <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">OBP</a> (.448) and <a href="/wiki/On-base_plus_slugging" title="On-base plus slugging">OPS</a> (.974) in <a href="/wiki/1886_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1886 St. Louis Browns season">1886</a> and finished fourth in <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a> in <a href="/wiki/1886_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1886 St. Louis Browns season">1886</a> (.334) and fifth in <a href="/wiki/1887_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1887 St. Louis Browns season">1887</a> (.357).<sup id="cite_ref-Bob_Caruthers_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bob_Caruthers-24">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  Outfielder <a href="/wiki/Tip_O%27Neill_(baseball)" title="Tip O&#39;Neill (baseball)">Tip O\'Neill</a> won the first batting <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">triple crown</a> in franchise history in 1887 and the only one in AA history.<sup id="cite_ref-Tip_O&#39;Neill_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tip_O&#39;Neill-25">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-O&#39;Neill_awards_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O&#39;Neill_awards-26">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MLB_triple_crowns_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB_triple_crowns-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  By winning the pennant, the Browns played the NL pennant winner <a href="/wiki/List_of_pre-World_Series_baseball_champions" title="List of pre-World Series baseball champions">in a predecessor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>.  The Browns twice met the Chicago White Stockings \xe2\x80\x93 the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a></i> prototype \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/1885_World_Series" title="1885 World Series">tying one</a> in a heated dispute and <a href="/wiki/1886_World_Series" title="1886 World Series">winning the other</a>, thus spurring the vigorous <a href="/wiki/Cardinals%E2%80%93Cubs_rivalry" title="Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry">St. Louis-Chicago rivalry</a> that ensues to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  During the franchise\'s ten seasons in the AA, they compiled an all-time league-high of 780 wins and .639 winning percentage.  They lost just 432 contests while tying 21 others.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Hornsby.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rogers_Hornsby.jpg/170px-Rogers_Hornsby.jpg" width="170" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rogers_Hornsby.jpg/255px-Rogers_Hornsby.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Rogers_Hornsby.jpg/340px-Rogers_Hornsby.jpg 2x" data-file-width="892" data-file-height="1494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Hornsby.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> won two <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crowns</a> as a Cardinal.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_triple_crowns_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB_triple_crowns-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The AA went bankrupt after the 1891 season and the Browns transferred to the National League.  This time, the club entered an era of stark futility.  Between <a href="/wiki/1892_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1892 St. Louis Browns season">1892</a> and <a href="/wiki/1919_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1919 St. Louis Cardinals season">1919</a>, St. Louis managed just five winning seasons, finished in last or next-to-last place sixteen times, and ended four seasons with 100 losses or more.  The <a href="/wiki/Nadir" title="Nadir">nadir</a> was the <a href="/wiki/1897_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1897 St. Louis Browns season">1897 season</a>: a 29\xe2\x80\x93102 record for a franchise-worst .221 winning percentage.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  St. Louis\' 84-67 finish <a href="/wiki/1899_St._Louis_Perfectos_season" title="1899 St. Louis Perfectos season">as the <b>Perfectos</b></a> would be the team\'s best finish between the AA era and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Breadon" title="Sam Breadon">Sam Breadon</a>\'s purchase of the team.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline1-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As the "Perfectos", the team wore their jersey with a cardinal red trim and sock striping.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline1-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Later that season, <i>St. Louis Republic</i> sportswriter Willie McHale included an account in a column of a female fan he heard remarking about the uniforms, "What a lovely shade of cardinal."  Fans liked the moniker "Cardinals" and, the next year, popularity for the nickname induced an official change to <b>Cardinals</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline1_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline1-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/1902_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1902 St. Louis Browns season">In 1902</a>, an American League team moved from <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a> into St. Louis, renamed themselves the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Browns" title="History of the St. Louis Browns"><b>St. Louis Browns</b></a> and built a new park <a href="/wiki/Sportsman%27s_Park" title="Sportsman&#39;s Park">on the site of the Cardinals\' old stadium</a>, striking a rivalry that lasted five decades.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  Breadon bought a minority interest in the Cardinals <a href="/wiki/1917_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1917 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1917</a> and <a href="/wiki/1919_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1919 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1919</a> Browns manager <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a> joined the Cardinals.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  The Cardinals\' first 28 seasons in the NL were a complete reversal of their stay in the AA \xe2\x80\x93 with a .406 winning percentage, they compiled 1,632 wins, 2,425 losses and 74 ties.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Breadon_era_.281920.E2.80.9352.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Breadon_era_(1920\xe2\x80\x9352)">Breadon era (1920\xe2\x80\x9352)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Breadon era (1920\xe2\x80\x9352)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Cardinals_(1920%E2%80%9352)" title="History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1920\xe2\x80\x9352)">History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1920\xe2\x80\x9352)</a></div>\n<p>St. Louis baseball commenced a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">renaissance</a>: <a href="/wiki/1926_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1926 St. Louis Cardinals season">since 1926</a> the Cardinals have won eleven World Series and nineteen NL pennants.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Breadon spurred this revival when bought out the majority stake in <a href="/wiki/1920_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1920 St. Louis Cardinals season">1920</a> and appointed Rickey as business manager, who expanded scouting, player development, and pioneered the <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">minor league</a> <a href="/wiki/Farm_team" title="Farm team">farm system</a>, filling the role of today\'s <a href="/wiki/General_manager_(baseball)" title="General manager (baseball)">general manager</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Branch_Rickey_career_highlights_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Branch_Rickey_career_highlights-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>  With <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> at second base, he claimed Triple Crowns in <a href="/wiki/1922_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1922 St. Louis Cardinals season">1922</a> and <a href="/wiki/1925_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1925 St. Louis Cardinals season">1925</a>, and the Cardinals won the <a href="/wiki/1926_World_Series" title="1926 World Series">1926 World Series</a>, their first.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_triple_crowns_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB_triple_crowns-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rogers_Hornsby_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogers_Hornsby-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  St. Louis then won <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_pennant_winners" title="List of National League pennant winners">the league</a> in <a href="/wiki/1928_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1928 St. Louis Cardinals season">1928</a>, <a href="/wiki/1930_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1930 St. Louis Cardinals season">1930</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1931_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1931 St. Louis Cardinals season">1931</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1931_World_Series" title="1931 World Series">1931 World Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline3_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline3-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stan_Musial_1957.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stan_Musial_1957.png/170px-Stan_Musial_1957.png" width="170" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stan_Musial_1957.png/255px-Stan_Musial_1957.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Stan_Musial_1957.png/340px-Stan_Musial_1957.png 2x" data-file-width="370" data-file-height="438" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stan_Musial_1957.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a> retired owning numerous <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> and team batting records.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gashouse_Gang" title="Gashouse Gang">Gashouse Gang</a> edition claimed the <a href="/wiki/1934_World_Series" title="1934 World Series">1934 World Series</a><sup id="cite_ref-Timeline3_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline3-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and the Cardinals amassed new thresholds of popularity far outside St. Louis via radio, which led to the coining of the term "<a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Nation" title="Cardinal Nation">Cardinal Nation</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Dizzy_and_the_Gashouse_Gang_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dizzy_and_the_Gashouse_Gang-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Dean" title="Dizzy Dean">Dizzy Dean</a> led the Gang, winning the 1934 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a>, and leading the NL multiple times in <a href="/wiki/Win_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Win (baseball)">wins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Innings_pitched" title="Innings pitched">innings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Complete_game" title="Complete game">complete games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shutouts_in_baseball" title="Shutouts in baseball">shutouts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dizzy_Dean_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dizzy_Dean-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Mize" title="Johnny Mize">Johnny Mize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Medwick" title="Joe Medwick">Joe Medwick</a> emerged as two power threats, with Medwick claiming the last Triple Crown for a Cardinal <a href="/wiki/1937_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1937 Major League Baseball season">in 1937</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB_triple_crowns_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB_triple_crowns-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timeline3_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline3-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Theme_of_the_Week,_December_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theme_of_the_Week,_December-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Johnny_Mize_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Mize-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Joe_Medwick_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Joe_Medwick-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1940s, a golden era emerged as Rickey\'s farm system became laden with such talent as <a href="/wiki/Marty_Marion" title="Marty Marion">Marty Marion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Marty_Marion_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marty_Marion-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Enos_Slaughter" title="Enos Slaughter">Enos Slaughter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Enos_Slaughter_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enos_Slaughter-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mort_Cooper" title="Mort Cooper">Mort Cooper</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Mort_Cooper_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mort_Cooper-43">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walker_Cooper" title="Walker Cooper">Walker Cooper</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Walker_Cooper_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walker_Cooper-44">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Stan_Musial_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stan_Musial-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Max_Lanier" title="Max Lanier">Max Lanier</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Max_Lanier_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Max_Lanier-46">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Whitey_Kurowski" title="Whitey Kurowski">Whitey Kurowski</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Whitey_Kurowski_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitey_Kurowski-47">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Red_Schoendienst" title="Red Schoendienst">Red Schoendienst</a><sup id="cite_ref-Red_Schoendienst_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Red_Schoendienst-48">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Beazley" title="Johnny Beazley">Johnny Beazley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnny_Beazley_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnny_Beazley-49">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>  It was one of the most successful decades in franchise history with 960 wins 580 losses for a winning percentage higher than any other Major League team at .623.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> With <a href="/wiki/Billy_Southworth" title="Billy Southworth">Billy Southworth</a> managing, they won the World Series in <a href="/wiki/1942_World_Series" title="1942 World Series">1942</a> and <a href="/wiki/1944_World_Series" title="1944 World Series">1944</a> (in the only all-St. Louis series against the <a href="/wiki/1944_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1944 St. Louis Browns season">Browns</a>), and won 105 or more games each in <a href="/wiki/1942_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1942 St. Louis Cardinals season">1942</a>, <a href="/wiki/1943_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1943 St. Louis Cardinals season">1943</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1942_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1942 St. Louis Cardinals season">1944</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>  Southworth\'s managerial winning percentage (.642) is St. Louis\' highest since the franchise joined the National League.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Billy_Southworth_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billy_Southworth-52">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>  Musial was considered the most consistent hitter of his era and most accomplished in team history, winning three MVPs and seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_batting_champions" title="List of Major League Baseball batting champions">batting titles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stan_Musial_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stan_Musial-45">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>  St. Louis then won the <a href="/wiki/1946_World_Series" title="1946 World Series">1946 World Series</a> on <a href="/wiki/Slaughter%27s_Mad_Dash" title="Slaughter&#39;s Mad Dash">Slaughter\'s Mad Dash</a> in Game 7.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>  Breadon was forced to sell the team <a href="/wiki/1947_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1947 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1947</a> but won six World Series and nine NL pennants as Cardinals owner.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline4_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline4-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>  They remained competitive, finishing .500 or better in thirteen of the next seventeen seasons, but fell short of winning the league or World Series <a href="/wiki/1964_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1964 St. Louis Cardinals season">until 1964</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Gussie_Busch_era_.281953.E2.80.9389.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gussie_Busch_era_(1953\xe2\x80\x9389)">Gussie Busch era (1953\xe2\x80\x9389)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gussie Busch era (1953\xe2\x80\x9389)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Cardinals_(1953%E2%80%9389)" title="History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1953\xe2\x80\x9389)">History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1953\xe2\x80\x9389)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bob_Gibson_1962.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bob_Gibson_1962.png/170px-Bob_Gibson_1962.png" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bob_Gibson_1962.png/255px-Bob_Gibson_1962.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/83/Bob_Gibson_1962.png 2x" data-file-width="302" data-file-height="401" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bob_Gibson_1962.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_award_winners_and_league_leaders" class="mw-redirect" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders">most decorated pitcher</a> in team history, won two <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bob_Gibson_player_page_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bob_Gibson_player_page-56">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/1953_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1953 St. Louis Cardinals season">1953</a> the <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> brewery <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_owners_and_executives" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals owners and executives">bought the Cardinals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gussie_Busch" title="Gussie Busch">August "Gussie" Busch</a> became team president,<sup id="cite_ref-Busch_buys_Cardinals_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Busch_buys_Cardinals-57">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> spurring the Browns\' departure in <a href="/wiki/1953_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1953 St. Louis Browns season">1953</a> to <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> to become the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Orioles" title="Baltimore Orioles">Orioles</a>, and making the Cardinals the only major league club in town.<sup id="cite_ref-St._Louis_Browns&#39;_move_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-St._Louis_Browns&#39;_move-58">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>  More success followed in the 1960s, starting with what is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Brock_for_Broglio" title="Brock for Broglio">most lopsided trades</a> in Major League history, as St. Louis received <a href="/wiki/Outfielder" title="Outfielder">outfielder</a> <a href="/wiki/Lou_Brock" title="Lou Brock">Lou Brock</a> from <a href="/wiki/1964_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1964 Chicago Cubs season">the Cubs</a> for pitcher <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Broglio" title="Ernie Broglio">Ernie Broglio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brock_for_Broglio_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brock_for_Broglio-59">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>  MVP third baseman <a href="/wiki/Ken_Boyer" title="Ken Boyer">Ken Boyer</a> and pitcher <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a> led the club to a <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series" title="1964 World Series">World Series win</a> the <a href="/wiki/1964_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1964 St. Louis Cardinals season">same year</a><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Curt_Flood" title="Curt Flood">Curt Flood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_White_(first_baseman)" title="Bill White (first baseman)">Bill White</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curt_Simmons" title="Curt Simmons">Curt Simmons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carlton" title="Steve Carlton">Steve Carlton</a> also made key contributions in this decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Bill_White_player_page_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bill_White_player_page-61">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steve_Carlton_player_page_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steve_Carlton_player_page-62">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Curt_Flood_player_page_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curt_Flood_player_page-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Curt_Simmons_player_page_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curt_Simmons_player_page-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/1967_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1967 St. Louis Cardinals season">In 1967</a>, new arrival <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Cepeda" title="Orlando Cepeda">Orlando Cepeda</a> won the MVP, helping to propel St. Louis to the <a href="/wiki/1967_World_Series" title="1967 World Series">World Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Orlando_Cepeda_player_page_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orlando_Cepeda_player_page-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>  The Cardinals won the league <a href="/wiki/1968_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1968 St. Louis Cardinals season">the following year</a> behind their Major League-leading 2.49 staff ERA<sup id="cite_ref-1968_Major_League_standings_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1968_Major_League_standings-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> in what was an all-round record-breaking season of <a href="/wiki/1968_Major_League_Baseball_season#The_Year_of_the_Pitcher" title="1968 Major League Baseball season">pitching dominance</a>.   Posting a modern-day record low ERA of 1.12 and striking out a one-game <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a>-record of 17,<sup id="cite_ref-1968_World_Series_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1968_World_Series-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Gibson won both the MVP and Cy Young awards that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Year_of_the_pitcher_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_of_the_pitcher-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> However, the Cardinals failed to repeat as <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Series" title="1968 World Series">World Series</a> champions, blowing a 3-1 lead to the underdog <a href="/wiki/1968_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1968 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a>.\n</p><p>In the 1970s, catcher/third baseman <a href="/wiki/Joe_Torre" title="Joe Torre">Joe Torre</a> and first baseman <a href="/wiki/Keith_Hern%C3%A1ndez" class="mw-redirect" title="Keith Hern\xc3\xa1ndez">Keith Hern\xc3\xa1ndez</a> each won MVPs, but the team\'s best finishes were second place and <a href="/wiki/1971_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1971 St. Louis Cardinals season">90 wins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline4_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline4-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Joe_Torre_player_page_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Joe_Torre_player_page-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Keith_Hern\xc3\xa1ndez_player_page_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keith_Hern\xc3\xa1ndez_player_page-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>  The team found their way back to the World Series the next decade, starting with manager <a href="/wiki/Whitey_Herzog" title="Whitey Herzog">Whitey Herzog</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Whiteyball" title="Whiteyball">Whiteyball</a> style of play and another trade that altered course of the franchise: <a href="/wiki/1982_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1982 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1982</a>, shortstop <a href="/wiki/Garry_Templeton" title="Garry Templeton">Garry Templeton</a> was shipped to the <a href="/wiki/1982_San_Diego_Padres_season" title="1982 San Diego Padres season">Padres</a> for fellow shortstop <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Smith" title="Ozzie Smith">Ozzie Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Herzog_manager_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Herzog_manager-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>  Widely regarded as one of the best defensive players in history, Smith ranks first all-time among shortstops in <a href="/wiki/List_of_Gold_Glove_Award_winners_at_shortstop" title="List of Gold Glove Award winners at shortstop">Gold Glove Awards</a> (13), <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star games</a> (15), <a href="/wiki/Assist_(baseball)" title="Assist (baseball)">assists</a> (8,375), and <a href="/wiki/Double_play" title="Double play">double plays</a> (1,590).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ozzie_Smith_player_page_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ozzie_Smith_player_page-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>  St. Louis won the <a href="/wiki/1982_World_Series" title="1982 World Series">1982 World Series</a> from the <a href="/wiki/1982_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="1982 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a> that fall.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>  The Cardinals again won the league in <a href="/wiki/1985_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1985 St. Louis Cardinals season">1985</a> and <a href="/wiki/1987_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1987 St. Louis Cardinals season">1987</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  In <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">the 1985 Series</a>, they faced-off with <a href="/wiki/Cardinals-Royals_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinals-Royals rivalry">cross-state</a> rivals <a href="/wiki/1985_Kansas_City_Royals_season" title="1985 Kansas City Royals season">Kansas City Royals</a> for the first time in a non-exhibition game, but they lost the series.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Bill_DeWitt_era_.281996.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bill_DeWitt_era_(1996\xe2\x80\x93present)">Bill DeWitt era (1996\xe2\x80\x93present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bill DeWitt era (1996\xe2\x80\x93present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Cardinals_(1990%E2%80%93present)" title="History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1990\xe2\x80\x93present)">History of the St. Louis Cardinals (1990\xe2\x80\x93present)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg/220px-Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg/330px-Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg/440px-Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chris_Carpenter_Close.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pitcher <a href="/wiki/Chris_Carpenter" title="Chris Carpenter">Chris Carpenter</a>, essential in two <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">World Series titles</a>, won 10 playoff games with a 3.00 postseason ERA.<sup id="cite_ref-Carpenter_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpenter-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg/170px-Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg/255px-Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg/340px-Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1476" data-file-height="2214" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Albert_Pujols_running_the_bases.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_award_winners_and_league_leaders" class="mw-redirect" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders">most accomplished</a> players in Cardinals\' history.</div></div></div>\n<p>After Gussie Busch died <a href="/wiki/1989_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1989 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1989</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">the brewery</a> took control<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> and hired Joe Torre to manage <a href="/wiki/1990_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1990 St. Louis Cardinals season">late in 1990</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Torre_manager_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Torre_manager-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> then sold the team to an investment group led by <a href="/wiki/William_DeWitt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William DeWitt, Jr.">William DeWitt, Jr.</a> <a href="/wiki/1995_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1995 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 1996</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Tony_La_Russa" title="Tony La Russa">Tony La Russa</a> replaced Torre in the spring of 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>  In 1998, <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGwire" title="Mark McGwire">Mark McGwire</a> competed with the <a href="/wiki/1998_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1998 Chicago Cubs season">Cubs\'</a> <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Sosa" title="Sammy Sosa">Sammy Sosa</a> for a barrage of home runs in their pursuit of the <a href="/wiki/1998_Major_League_Baseball_home_run_record_chase" title="1998 Major League Baseball home run record chase">single-season home run record</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>  From <a href="/wiki/2000_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2000 St. Louis Cardinals season">2000</a> to <a href="/wiki/2013_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2013 St. Louis Cardinals season">2013</a>, the Cardinals reestablished their way to the top with ten playoff appearances, four <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_pennant_winners" title="List of National League pennant winners">NL pennants</a>, two World Series titles and 1,274 regular season wins against 993 losses for a .560 winning percentage, leading the National League and second in MLB only to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  With the addition of <a href="/wiki/Jim_Edmonds" title="Jim Edmonds">Jim Edmonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Rolen" title="Scott Rolen">Scott Rolen</a>, the Cardinals featured three prominent sluggers and defenders nicknamed "MV3;"<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Pujols won three MVPs and hit .328 with 445 home runs in his Cardinals career.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/2004_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2004 St. Louis Cardinals season">In 2004</a>, playoff stalwart <a href="/wiki/Chris_Carpenter" title="Chris Carpenter">Chris Carpenter</a>\'s 3.09 ERA and 15 wins<sup id="cite_ref-Carpenter_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carpenter-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> helped power the team to a <a href="/wiki/2004_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2004 Major League Baseball season">major-league best</a> 105 wins and take the <a href="/wiki/2004_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2004 National League Championship Series">NL pennant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/2006_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2006 St. Louis Cardinals season">In 2006</a>, beset with injuries and inconsistency,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> they won the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">World Series</a>, beating Detroit in five games to set an all-time record-low of 83 wins for a World Series winner.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Timeline6_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline6-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/2009_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2009 St. Louis Cardinals season">In 2009</a>, the Cardinals reached 10,000 wins, dating to when they first played in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> (AA).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  St. Louis returned to the playoffs <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">in 2011</a>, first surmounting the largest games-won deficit after 130 games (at 10.5) to upstage the <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2011 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> on the final day for the wild card playoff berth.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  In Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">World Series</a>, Pujols became just the third player to hit three home runs in a World Series game.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  In Game 6, third baseman <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a> each tied the score on the Cardinals\'  final strike \xe2\x80\x93 the first such occurrence in any game in MLB history \xe2\x80\x93 and St. Louis defeated the <a href="/wiki/2012_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2012 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> later that game with a <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> from Freese.<sup id="cite_ref-Dicomo1_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dicomo1-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>  After winning that Series, La Russa retired and became the only manager to do so after winning a title.  He also finished with the most wins for managers in franchise history with 1,408.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>La Russa\'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Matheny" title="Mike Matheny">Mike Matheny</a>, helped extend St. Louis\' playoff run as he became the first manager in the <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_season#Division_play" title="1969 Major League Baseball season">division play</a> era to guide the Cardinals to the NLCS and playoffs in his first two seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>  In <a href="/wiki/2014_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2014 St. Louis Cardinals season">2014</a>, the Cardinals extended their NLCS streak to 4, with their 3-1 series victory over the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Dodgers</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/2014_National_League_Division_Series" title="2014 National League Division Series">NLDS</a>. Ten days after being eliminated from the postseason by the San Francisco Giants, rookie outfielder <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Taveras" title="Oscar Taveras">Oscar Taveras</a> was killed in a car accident while traveling to his hometown Puerto Plata in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>  On November 17, they acquired <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> right-fielder <a href="/wiki/Jason_Heyward" title="Jason Heyward">Jason Heyward</a> (who had just come off a <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove">Gold Glove</a>-winning season) to replace Taveras.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> On June 16, 2015, the <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Justice Department</a> started an investigation on the Cardinals for possibly hacking the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a>. The hacking incident was perpetrated by Scouting Director Chris Correa.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> For the first time since the <a href="/wiki/2007_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2007 St. Louis Cardinals season">2007</a>&#8211;<a href="/wiki/2008_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2008 St. Louis Cardinals season">2008</a> seasons, the Cardinals missed the playoffs in consecutive years, <a href="/wiki/2016_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2016 St. Louis Cardinals season">2016</a>&#8211;<a href="/wiki/2017_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2017 St. Louis Cardinals season">2017</a>.\n</p><p>On July 14th, 2018 following an 8-2 loss to the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a>, the St. Louis Cardinals announced they had dismissed manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Matheny" title="Mike Matheny">Mike Matheny</a> after 6 and a half seasons as team skipper. They named <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shildt" title="Mike Shildt">Mike Shildt</a> interim manager and eventually manager.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ballpark">Ballpark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ballpark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Busch_Stadium" title="Busch Stadium">Busch Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busch_Memorial_Stadium" title="Busch Memorial Stadium">Busch Memorial Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sportsman%27s_Park" title="Sportsman&#39;s Park">Sportsman\'s Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robison_Field" title="Robison Field">Robison Field</a></div>\n<p>The Cardinals play their home games at Busch Stadium (also referred to as <i>New Busch Stadium</i> or <i>Busch III</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_St._Louis" title="Downtown St. Louis">downtown St. Louis</a>, straddling 7th and Clark near the intersection of I<a href="/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System" title="Interstate Highway System">nterstates</a> <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">64</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">70</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>  The stadium opened for the <a href="/wiki/2006_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2006 St. Louis Cardinals season">2006 season</a> at a cost of $411 million and holds a normal capacity of 46,861.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>  The Cardinals finished their inaugural season in the new Busch Stadium by winning the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006 World Series</a>, the first team since the 1923 <a href="/wiki/1923_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1923 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a> to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>  This open-air <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadium</a> emulates the HOK Sport (now <a href="/wiki/Populous_(company)" title="Populous (company)">Populous</a>)-designed "<a href="/wiki/Baseball_park#retro-classic_ballparks" title="Baseball park">retro-style</a>" baseball-only parks built since the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>  The open panoramic perspective over the outfield wall offers a remarkable view of St. Louis\' downtown skyline featuring the distinctive <a href="/wiki/Gateway_Arch" title="Gateway Arch">Gateway Arch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>  A replica of <a href="/wiki/Eads_Bridge" title="Eads Bridge">Eads Bridge</a> spans the entrance to the park on the third base side, while the <a href="/wiki/Statue" title="Statue">statue</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a> arises in front of that entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>  Other statues at the corner of 8th and Clark include Hall of Famers <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozzie_Smith" title="Ozzie Smith">Ozzie Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Sisler" title="George Sisler">George Sisler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cool_Papa_Bell" title="Cool Papa Bell">Cool Papa Bell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Buck" title="Jack Buck">Jack Buck</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to increased demand, Game 7 of the <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Series" title="2011 World Series">2011 World Series</a> accommodated a baseball record of 47,399 by increasing the number of <a href="/wiki/Standing_room_only" class="mw-redirect" title="Standing room only">standing room only</a> tickets.  The attendance record for any sporting event is 48,263, in a 2013 <a href="/wiki/Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Football">Association Football</a> (soccer) <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendly match</a> between <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City F.C.</a>, made possible by on field seating.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>  The largest attendance (53,000) of any event at Busch belongs to <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> during a concert from their <a href="/wiki/U2_360%C2%B0_Tour" title="U2 360\xc2\xb0 Tour">360\xc2\xb0 Tour</a> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Ballpark_Village" title="St. Louis Ballpark Village">Ballpark Village</a>, a mixed-use development located across Clark Street from Busch Stadium, is targeted to enhance the ballpark goers\' experience.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  Phase 1 of the development, completed for the start of the 2014 season, includes <a href="/wiki/Entertainment" title="Entertainment">entertainment</a> venues, <a href="/wiki/Restaurant" title="Restaurant">restaurants</a>, and retail.  Anchored by Cardinals Nation (which includes the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_Hall_of_Fame_Museum" title="St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum">Cardinals Hall of Fame</a>, a two-story Cardinals-themed restaurant and rooftop seating for 300+ fans with views of the field across the street), a 20,000 sq ft Budweiser Brew House, FOX Sports Midwest Live! and <a href="/wiki/Professional_Bull_Riders" title="Professional Bull Riders">PBR</a>, the $100 million phase 1 development of Ballpark Village is intended to be a gathering space throughout the year, not just during the baseball season.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Previous_ballparks">Previous ballparks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Previous ballparks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Busch Stadium is the Cardinals\' fourth home ballpark and the third to bear that name.  The Cardinals\' original home ballpark was <a href="/wiki/Sportsman%27s_Park" title="Sportsman&#39;s Park">Sportsman\'s Park</a> from 1882 to 1892 when they played in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> and were known as the Browns.  <a href="/wiki/1893_St._Louis_Browns_season" title="1893 St. Louis Browns season">In 1893</a>, the Browns moved to a new ballpark five blocks northwest of Sportsman\'s Park which would serve as their home from 1893 to 1920.  The new park was originally called New Sportsman\'s Park but became more commonly referred to as <a href="/wiki/Robison_Field" title="Robison Field">Robison Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline1_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline1-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Midway through the 1920 season the Cardinals abandoned Robison Field and returned to the original Sportsman\'s Park and became tenants of their American League rivals, the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a>.  In 1953, the <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch Brewery</a> purchased the Cardinals and the new owner subsequently also purchased Sportsman\'s Park from the Browns and renamed it Busch Stadium, later becoming Busch I. The Browns then left St. Louis for <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a> after the season. The Cardinals built <a href="/wiki/Busch_Memorial_Stadium" title="Busch Memorial Stadium">Busch Memorial Stadium</a>, or Busch II, in downtown St. Louis, opened it during the 1966 season and played there until 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline4_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline4-55">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> It was built as the <a href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_stadium" title="Multi-purpose stadium">multi-purpose stadium</a> home of both the baseball Cardinals and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_St._Louis_Cardinals_(NFL)" title="History of the St. Louis Cardinals (NFL)">NFL football Cardinals</a>, who are now the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Cardinals" title="Arizona Cardinals">Arizona Cardinals</a>. The current Busch Stadium was constructed adjacent to, and partly atop, the site of Busch Memorial Stadium.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spring_training">Spring training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Spring training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Cardinals home field in <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> is <a href="/wiki/Roger_Dean_Stadium" title="Roger Dean Stadium">Roger Dean Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jupiter,_Florida" title="Jupiter, Florida">Jupiter, Florida</a>.  They share the complex, which opened in 1998, with the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Marlins" title="Miami Marlins">Miami Marlins</a>.  Before moving to Jupiter, the Cardinals hosted spring training at <a href="/wiki/Al_Lang_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Lang Field">Al Lang Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg, Florida</a> from 1937 to 1997.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regular_season_home_attendance">Regular season home attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Regular season home attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Cardinals have exceeded the attendance total of 3 million every season since 2004.\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="10">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n<table cellpadding="1" style="width:300px; font-size:90%; border:2px solid #C4203B;">\n\n<tbody><tr
