season">2017</a>\n</td>\n<td>3,448,337\n</td>\n<td>42,572\n</td>\n<td>2nd\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_uniforms">Logos and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Logos and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Cardinals have had few logos throughout their history, although those logos have evolved over time.  The first logo associated with the Cardinals was an interlocking "SL" that appeared on the team\'s caps and or sleeves as early as 1900.  Those early uniforms usually featured the name "St. Louis" on white home and gray road uniforms which both had <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(color)" title="Cardinal (color)">cardinal red</a> accents.  In 1920, the "SL" largely disappeared from the team\'s uniforms, and for the next 20 years the team wore caps that were white with red striping and a red bill.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Louis_Cardinals_1929-1948_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/02/St_Louis_Cardinals_1929-1948_logo.png/220px-St_Louis_Cardinals_1929-1948_logo.png" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/02/St_Louis_Cardinals_1929-1948_logo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Louis_Cardinals_1929-1948_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The original "birds on the bat" logo, which first appeared in 1922.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1922, the Cardinals wore uniforms for the first time that featured the two familiar <a href="/wiki/Northern_cardinal" title="Northern cardinal">cardinal</a> birds perched on a <a href="/wiki/Baseball_bat" title="Baseball bat">baseball bat</a> over the name "Cardinals" with the letter "C" of the word hooked over the bat.  The concept of the birds originated after <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_owners_and_executives" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals owners and executives">general manager</a> <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a> noticed a colorful cardboard arrangement featuring cardinal birds on a table in a <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(U.S.A.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Church (U.S.A.)">Presbyterian</a> <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ferguson,_Missouri" title="Ferguson, Missouri">Ferguson, Missouri</a>, at which he was speaking.  The arrangement\'s production was by a woman named Allie May Schmidt.  Schmidt\'s father, a <a href="/wiki/Graphic_designer" title="Graphic designer">graphic designer</a>, helped Ricky make the logo a familiar staple on Cardinals uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>  Colloquially referred to as the "birds on the bat", it initially appeared with the birds perched on a black bat and "Cardinals" in printed letters.  An alternate version of this logo with "St. Louis" replacing "Cardinals" appeared in 1930 and was the primary logo in 1931 and 1932 before "Cardinals" returned.  In 1940, the now-familiar "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>" logo was introduced on the team\'s caps.  The interlocking "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>" has undergone several slight modifications over the years but has appeared on the team\'s caps every year since.  The first appearance of the "STL" in 1940 coincided with the introduction of navy blue as a uniform color.  From 1940 until 1955, the team wore navy blue caps with red bills and a red interlocking "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>" while the jerseys featured both cardinal red and navy blue accents.  In 1951, the "birds on the bat" logo was changed to feature a yellow baseball bat.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardsunis_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardsunis-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Louis_Cardinals_1998-present_logo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/St_Louis_Cardinals_1998-present_logo.png/220px-St_Louis_Cardinals_1998-present_logo.png" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b4/St_Louis_Cardinals_1998-present_logo.png 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Louis_Cardinals_1998-present_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The current "birds on the bat" logo introduced in 1998 (although variations of this have been used since 1957).</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1956, the Cardinals changed their caps to solid blue with a red "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>", removing the red bill.  Also, for that season only, the Cardinals wore a script "Cardinals" wordmark on their uniforms excluding the "birds on the bat."  An updated version of the "birds on the bat" logo returned in 1957 with the word "Cardinals" written in cursive beneath the bat.  In 1962, the Cardinals became the first National League team to display players\' names on the back of their jerseys.  In 1964, while retaining their blue caps for road games, the Cardinals changed their <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://exhibits.baseballhalloffame.org/dressed_to_the_nines/detail_page.asp?fileName=nl_1964_stlouis.gif&amp;Entryid=1045">home caps</a> to all red with a white interlocking "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>".  The next year, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://exhibits.baseballhalloffame.org/dressed_to_the_nines/detail_page.asp?fileName=nl_1965_stlouis.gif&amp;Entryid=1065">red caps</a> were the only cap worn by the team full-time. In 1967, the birds on the bat emblem on the jersey was again tweaked, making the birds more realistic and changing the position of their tails relative to the bat and this version remained on all Cardinals game jerseys through 1997.\n</p><p>In 1971, following the trend in baseball at the time, the Cardinals replaced the traditional flannel front-button shirts and pants with belts with new pullover knit jerseys and beltless elastic waist pants. In 1973, the crew-neck collar became a V-neck. Another trend in baseball led the Cardinals to change their road uniforms from gray to light blue from 1976 to 1984. In 1992, the Cardinals returned to wearing traditional button-down shirts and pants with belts.  That same year, they also brought back the all-navy cap with a red "<span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">StL</span>" on the road (which were last worn in 1964) only while wearing the same red and white cap for home games only.  \nIn 1998, the "birds on the bat" was updated for the first time in 30 years with more detailed birds and bolder letters.  That year, St. Louis introduced a cap featuring a single cardinal bird perched on a bat worn only on Sunday home games.  The new birds on the bat design was modified again the next year, with yellow beaks and white eyes replacing the red beaks and yellow eyes of the 1998 version.  Uniform numbers also returned to the front of the jerseys in 1999 after a two-year absence.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardsunis_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardsunis-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 16, 2012, the Cardinals unveiled a new alternate uniform to be worn at home games on Saturdays beginning with the 2013 season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The text near this tag is dated. (April 2013)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>  The modified jersey, cream-colored with red trim on the sleeves and down the front, was the first since 1932 in which "St. Louis" will be used instead of "Cardinals" and retained the "birds on the bat."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> 2013 also saw the team adopt their red caps as their main uniform for both home and away games; the navy cap was retained as an alternate, used mainly against other red-capped teams.   Over the years, the Cardinals have released various marketing logos depicting <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphized" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthropomorphized">anthropomorphized</a> cardinals in a pitching stance, swinging a baseball bat, or wearing a baseball cap that never became part of the game uniform.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardsunis_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardsunis-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fans">Fans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Fans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Nation" title="Cardinal Nation">Cardinal Nation</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots">Mascots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mascots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fredbird" title="Fredbird">Fredbird</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rally_Squirrel" title="Rally Squirrel">Rally Squirrel</a></div>\n<p>The team mascot is an anthropomorphic cardinal wearing the team\'s uniform named <a href="/wiki/Fredbird" title="Fredbird">Fredbird</a>. He is assisted by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://stlouis.cardinals.mlb.com/stl/fan_forum/team_fredbird.jsp">Team Fredbird</a>, a group of eleven women who entertain fans from the field and on top of the dugouts.\n</p><p>While unofficial, the Rally Squirrel became an unexpected phenomenon during the 2011 postseason.  Making its "debut" in Game 3 of the <a href="/wiki/2011_National_League_Division_Series" title="2011 National League Division Series">NLDS</a> on Oct 4, a squirrel ran across home plate in the middle of a pitch from <a href="/wiki/Roy_Oswalt" title="Roy Oswalt">Roy Oswalt</a> of the Phillies to the Cardinals\' <a href="/wiki/Skip_Schumaker" title="Skip Schumaker">Skip Schumaker</a>.  The Cardinals would win Game 4 and subsequently Game 5 (Oct. 7) in Philadelphia to advance to the NLCS, symbolizing the squirrel\'s "role" in the victory.  The squirrel was popularized as "Buschie the Rally Squirrel"<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> As a tribute to the popularity of the squirrel, a small depiction of the Rally Squirrel is also included on the official <a href="/wiki/World_Series_ring" title="World Series ring">World Series rings</a> the team received. It shows up under the "STL" logo on the side of the ring.\n</p><p>Fredbird sparked controversy in May 2015, when he was asked by a fan for a photograph and handed him a sign that said "Police Lives Matter". The team later claimed that Fredbird should not be involved in any political activity or social commentary.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago_Cubs">Chicago Cubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Chicago Cubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardinals%E2%80%93Cubs_rivalry" title="Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry">Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry</a></div>\n<p>The Cardinals\xe2\x80\x93Cubs rivalry refers to games between the Cardinals and the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>. The rivalry is also known as the <b>Downstate Illinois rivalry</b> or the <b>I-55 Series</b> (in earlier years as the <b>Route 66 Series</b>) as both cities are located along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_55" title="Interstate 55">Interstate 55</a> (which itself succeeded the famous <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_66" title="U.S. Route 66">U.S. Route 66</a>). The Cubs lead the series 1,134\xe2\x80\x931,103 through June 22, 2016, while the Cardinals lead in <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> pennants with 19 against the Cubs\' 17. The Cubs have won 11 of those pennants in Major League Baseball\'s Modern Era (1901\xe2\x80\x93present), while all 19 of the Cardinals\' pennants have been won since 1926. The Cardinals also have an edge when it comes to <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> successes, having won 11 championships to the Cubs\' 3. Games featuring the Cardinals and Cubs see numerous visiting fans in either <a href="/wiki/Busch_Stadium" title="Busch Stadium">Busch Stadium</a> in St. Louis or  <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> in Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> When the National League split into two and then three divisions, the Cardinals and Cubs remained together. This has added excitement to several pennant races over the years.  The Cardinals and Cubs have played each other once in the postseason, when the Cubs beat the Cardinals 3 games to 1 in the 2015 National League Division Series.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Executives_and_club_officials">Executives and club officials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Executives and club officials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_owners_and_executives" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals owners and executives">List of St. Louis Cardinals owners and executives</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership_and_valuation">Ownership and valuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ownership and valuation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An investment group led by <a href="/wiki/William_DeWitt,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William DeWitt, Jr.">William DeWitt, Jr.</a> owns the St. Louis Cardinals, having bought the team from <a href="/wiki/Anheuser-Busch" title="Anheuser-Busch">Anheuser-Busch</a> (AB) in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>  As with other periods of the Cardinals\' transaction history, doubt loomed as to whether the purchaser would keep the team in St. Louis, due to the city\'s status as a "small market", which appears to handicap a club\'s competitiveness.  Such was the case when <a href="/wiki/Sam_Breadon" title="Sam Breadon">Sam Breadon</a> put the Cardinals up for sale in 1947: <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_League_presidents" title="List of National League presidents">then-NL President</a> <a href="/wiki/Ford_Frick" title="Ford Frick">Ford Frick</a> proposed moving the Cardinals to <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Baseball&#39;s_Sign_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baseball&#39;s_Sign-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>  When AB placed the Cardinals for sale in 1995, they publicly expressed intention to find a buyer who would keep the club in St. Louis.<sup id="cite_ref-Cards_put_up_for_sale_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cards_put_up_for_sale-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>  In March 1996, AB sold the team for $147 million to a partnership headed by Southwest Bank\'s <a href="/wiki/Drew_Baur" title="Drew Baur">Drew Baur</a>, Hanser and DeWitt, Jr.<sup id="cite_ref-Baseball&#39;s_Sign_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baseball&#39;s_Sign-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>  Civic Center Redevelopment, a subsidiary of AB, held the parking garages and adjacent property and also transferred them to the Baur ownership group.<sup id="cite_ref-Judd2002_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Judd2002-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>  Baur\'s group then sold the garages to another investment group, lowering the net franchise purchase price to about $100 million, about $10 million less than <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_World" title="Financial World">Financial World</a>\'s</i> value of the team at the time $110 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Cards_put_up_for_sale_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cards_put_up_for_sale-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cards_owners&#39;_value_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cards_owners&#39;_value-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Current <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> owners <a href="/wiki/Bob_Castellini" title="Bob Castellini">Bob Castellini</a> and brothers Thomas Williams and W. Joseph Williams Jr. each once owned a stake in the Cardinals dating back to the Baur-DeWitt group\'s purchase of the team.  To allow their purchase of the Reds in 2005, the rest of the group bought out Castellini\'s and the Williams brothers\' shares, totaling an estimated thirteen percent.  At that time, the <i>Forbes</i> valued the Cardinals at about $370 million.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>  However, after reabsorbing that stake into the remainder of the group, they decided to make it available to new investors in 2010.  Amid later allegations that the Cardinals owed the city profit shares, DeWitt revealed that their profitability had not reached the threshold to trigger that obligation.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_annual_financial_records">Recent annual financial records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Recent annual financial records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As of 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> valued the Cardinals seventh among 30 MLB franchises. Their estimated value of $1.90 billion was an increase of $100 million from the season before, when they ranked seventh. St. Louis\' revenue in 2018 was $319 million, up $9 million. Their <a href="/wiki/Earnings_before_interest_and_taxes" title="Earnings before interest and taxes">Operating income</a> was $40.0 million.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes2018_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2018-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Cardinals\' deal with <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Midwest" title="Fox Sports Midwest">Fox Sports Midwest</a>, signed in 2015, begins in 2018, and is worth $1 billion through 2032.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes2016_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes2016-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2015_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2015-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2014_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2014-133">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2013_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2013-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, <i>Forbes</i> valued the Cardinals at $820 million and opined previously that they play "in the best single-team baseball market in the country and are among the league\'s leaders in television ratings and attendance every season."<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes2013_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes2013-134">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>  Concurrent with the growth of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, the Cardinals value has increased significantly since the Baur-DeWitt purchase. In 2000, the franchise was valued at $219 million,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> a growth rate of 374% through 2014. The franchise\'s value grew 12.7% from 2013 to 2014.\nThe <i>Forbes</i> methodology of team values are enterprise values (equity plus net debt) that include the economics of the ballpark but exclude the value of real estate itself. Forbes does not include the value of team-owned regional sports networks. The league\'s ownership in Major League Baseball Advanced Media (100%) and the MLB Network (67%) and league\'s investment portfolio are included in our values. In total, these three assets constitute about $425 million in value for each team. Revenue and operating income (earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization) measure cash in versus cash out (not accrual accounting) for the 2017 season. Their figures include the post-season and are net of revenue sharing and stadium debt payments. Revenues include the pro-rated upfront bonuses networks pay teams as well as proceeds from non-MLB events at the ballpark. The non-recurring $18 million each team received in 2017 from the sale of a stake in BamTech to Walt Disney was excluded, as were profits or losses from team-owned RSNs.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="1" style="width:850px; font-size:90%; border:2px solid #C4203B;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="text-align:center; href="#cite_note-143">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and considered a smashing success with the first phase of the project totaling 120,000 square feet (11,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The Cardinals own three of their <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a> affililiates:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Springfield_Cardinals" title="Springfield Cardinals">Springfield Cardinals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_League" title="Texas League">Texas League</a> (AA)<sup id="cite_ref-MinLgFranc_146-0" class="reference"><a title="Florida State League">Florida State League</a> (High-A)<sup id="cite_ref-MinLgFranc_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MinLgFranc-146">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a GM on Sep. 27, 2017)</li>\n<li>Director of Player Personnel:  Matt Slater</li>\n<li>Director, Baseball Administration:  John Vuch</li>\n<li>Senior Medical Advisor:  Barry Weinberg</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Finance and Administration<sup id="cite_ref-Frontoffice_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontoffice-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Sr. Vice President and <a href="/wiki/Chief_financial_officer" title="Chief financial officer">CFO</a>:  Brad Wood</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Event Services and Merchandising<sup id="cite_ref-Frontoffice_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontoffice-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Vice President, Event Services and Merchandising:  Vicki Bryant</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Stadium Operations<sup id="cite_ref-Frontoffice_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontoffice-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Vice President, Stadium Operations:  Matt Gifford</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Ticket Sales, Marketing &amp; Corporate Sales<sup id="cite_ref-Frontoffice_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frontoffice-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>\n<ul><li>Sr. Vice President of Sales &amp; Marketing:  Dan Farrell</li>\n<li>Vice President, Corp. Marketing &amp; Stadium Entertainment:  Thane van Breusegen</li>\n<li>Vice President, Ticket Sales and Services:  Joe Strohm</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_roll">Managerial roll">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_managers" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals managers">List of St. Louis Cardinals managers</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Manager_(baseball)" title="Manager (baseball)">Field managers</a> with one or more years managing, and the current manager are included here.<sup id="cite_ref-Cardinals_franchise_index_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cardinals_franchise_index-6">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;;">Dates\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;;">Name\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;;">W-L Record\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;;">%\n</th>\n<th Major League Baseball team rosters">All MLB rosters</a></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaching_staff">Coaching staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Coaching staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_coaches" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals coaches">List of St. Louis Cardinals coaches</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selected_individual_achievements_and_awards">Selected individual achievements and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Selected individual achievements and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders">St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_team_records" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Cardinals team records">St. Louis Cardinals team records</a></div>\n<ul><li><b>Darryl Kile Award:</b> Two awards are presented each year, one to a St. Louis Cardinal and one to a Houston Astro, each of whom exemplifies Kile\'s virtues of being "a good teammate, a great friend, a fine father and a humble man." The winner is selected by each local chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Writers%27_Association_of_America" title="Baseball Writers&#39; Association of America">Baseball Writers\' Association of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Darryl_Kile_Award_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Darryl_Kile_Award-174">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> See: <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_award_winners_and_league_leaders#Darryl_Kile_Good_Guy_Award" title="St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders">St. Louis Cardinals award winners and league leaders \xc2\xa7&#160;Darryl Kile Good Guy Award</a>.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_no-hitters" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals no-hitters">No-hitters</a>:</b> Cardinal pitchers have thrown 10 <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitters</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ted_Breitenstein" title="Ted Breitenstein">Ted Breitenstein</a> (1891), <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Haines" title="Jesse Haines">Jesse Haines</a> (1924), <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dean_(baseball)" title="Paul Dean (baseball)">Paul Dean</a> (1934), <a href="/wiki/Lon_Warneke" title="Lon Warneke">Lon Warneke</a> (1941), <a href="/wiki/Ray_Washburn" title="Ray Washburn">Ray Washburn</a> (1968), <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a> (1971), <a href="/wiki/Bob_Forsch" title="Bob Forsch">Bob Forsch</a> (1978 and 1983), <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Jim%C3%A9nez_(baseball)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Jim\xc3\xa9nez (baseball)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Jim\xc3\xa9nez</a> (1999), and <a href="/wiki/Bud_Smith" title="Bud Smith">Bud Smith</a> (2001). The Cardinals have never been involved in a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a>, win or lose.</li>\n<li><b>Cy Young Awards:</b> Two Cardinal pitchers have won <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a> in 1968 and 1970, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Carpenter" title="Chris Carpenter">Chris Carpenter</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-175">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>MVP Awards:</b> 16 different Cardinal players have won a total of 20 <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Major League Baseball Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player awards</a>, the most recent being <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> in 2009. Pujols and <a href="/wiki/Stan_Musial" title="Stan Musial">Stan Musial</a> have collected the most MVPs with three apiece.  Bob Gibson won both the Cy Young Award and the MVP award in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-175">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The Cardinals are second only to the New York Yankees\' 22 MVP awards.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Rookie of the Year:</b> Six Cardinals have won the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">Rookie of the Year award</a>: <a href="/wiki/Wally_Moon" title="Wally Moon">Wally Moon</a> in 1954, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Virdon" title="Bill Virdon">Bill Virdon</a> in 1955, <a href="/wiki/Bake_McBride" title="Bake McBride">Bake McBride</a> in 1974, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Coleman" title="Vince Coleman">Vince Coleman</a> in 1985, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Worrell" title="Todd Worrell">Todd Worrell</a> in 1986, and Albert Pujols in 2001.</li>\n<li><b>Hitting for the cycle:</b> 20 Cardinal players have <a href="/wiki/Hitting_for_the_cycle" title="Hitting for the cycle">hit for the cycle</a>, the most recent being <a href="/wiki/Mark_Grudzielanek" title="Mark Grudzielanek">Mark Grudzielanek</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Triple Crown:</b> Four of the 16 batting <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crowns</a> in the major leagues (including three of only six in the National League) were by Cardinals. <a href="/wiki/Tip_O%27Neill_(baseball)" title="Tip O&#39;Neill (baseball)">Tip O\'Neill</a> won the only <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> Triple Crown and the first in franchise history in 1887.  <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> became the only two-time winner in NL history when he did it in 1922 and 1925 (<a href="/wiki/Ted_Williams" title="Ted Williams">Ted Williams</a> won two AL Triple Crowns). <a href="/wiki/Joe_Medwick" title="Joe Medwick">Joe Medwick</a>\'s Triple Crown in 1937 is the last in the history of the National League.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Hornsby\'s 1925 numbers led the entire major leagues, making him one of only five players to have won this expanded Triple Crown.</li>\n<li><b>Home runs and RBI in a game:</b> Jim Bottomley drove in 12 runs against <a href="/wiki/1924_Brooklyn_Robins_season" title="1924 Brooklyn Robins season">Brooklyn</a> on September 16, 1924, an <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_single-game_records" title="List of Major League Baseball single-game records">all-time MLB single-game record</a> that still stands.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>  On September 7, 1993, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Whiten" title="Mark Whiten">Mark Whiten</a> tied that record and another MLB single-game record <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_single-game_home_run_leaders" title="List of Major League Baseball single-game home run leaders">with four home runs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>2 Grand Slams in a single inning:</b> <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Tat%C3%ADs" title="Fernando Tat\xc3\xads">Fernando Tat\xc3\xads</a> is the only player in Major League history to hit two <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Slam (baseball)">grand slam</a> home runs in the same inning, on April 23, 1999.  Both were against <a href="/wiki/Chan_Ho_Park" title="Chan Ho Park">Chan Ho Park</a> of the Dodgers.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_captains">Team captains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Team captains">edit</a><span title="Terry Moore (baseball)">Terry Moore</a> 1942\xe2\x80\x931948</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ken_Boyer" title="Ken Boyer">Ken Boyer</a> 1959\xe2\x80\x931965</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hall_of_Famers">Hall of Famers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" style="margin: 1em auto;display:none">\n<caption>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td>\n<td width="50">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>Players and managers listed in <b>bold</b> are depicted on their Hall of Fame plaques wearing a Browns or Cardinals cap insignia.</li>\n<li>* Has no insignia on his cap due to playing at a time when caps bore no insignia.</li>\n<li>** Wears no cap.</li>\n<li>\xe2\x80\xa0 Played for the AL St. Louis Browns, but not the NL St. Louis club.  Because of their status as the only Major League team remaining in St. Louis, the Cardinals franchise chose to honor Sisler as a St. Louis-based player.</li>\n<li>\xc2\xa7 Wears a Cardinals insignia but the Hall of Fame recognizes the Chicago Cubs as his primary team.</li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li>\n<li class="mw-empty-elt"></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Louis_Cardinals_Hall_of_Fame_Museum">St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_Hall_of_Fame_Museum" title="St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum">St. Louis Cardinals Hall of Fame Museum</a></div>\n<p>In 2014, the Cardinals announced the reopening of the franchise Hall of Fame after a 6-year hiatus.  A formal selection process recognizes former players as Cardinals Hall of Famers each year.  To be eligible for election, a player must have been a member of the Cardinals for at least three seasons.  The team initially released the names of 22 former players and personnel included in the inaugural class of <a href="/wiki/2014_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2014 St. Louis Cardinals season">2014</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> There are now 40 members of the Cardinals Hall of Fame.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers</a></div>\n<p>The Cardinals have retired 12 total jersey numbers\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93second in MLB only to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees#Retired_numbers" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a>\' 21\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93in honoring 14 total former players and club personnel on the left field wall at <a href="/wiki/Busch_Stadium" title="Busch Stadium">Busch Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>  A 15th, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, is honored by all MLB teams.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>  During the time <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers Hornsby</a> had played, the Cardinals did not have any numbers on their uniforms. This practice had begun with the Cleveland Indians in 1920. Thus, Hornsby had no number to retire.\n</p>\n<table style="white-space:nowrap"><tbody><tr><td>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:CardsRetiredSTL.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/CardsRetiredSTL.PNG/100px-CardsRetiredSTL.PNG" width="100" height="81" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/69/CardsRetiredSTL.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="95" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Rogers_Hornsby" title="Rogers Hornsby">Rogers<br />Hornsby</a><br />2B, Mgr<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap">1975</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:CardsRetired85.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/CardsRetired85.PNG/100px-CardsRetired85.PNG" width="100" height="81" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/CardsRetired85.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="95" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Gussie_Busch" title="Gussie Busch">Gussie<br />Busch</a><br />Owner<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Retired <span style="white-space:nowrap">1984</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table style="float:left; text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:CardsRetiredMic.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/CardsRetiredMic.png/100px-CardsRetiredMic.png" width="100" height="81" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/CardsRetiredMic.png 1.5x" data-file-width="117" data-file-height="95" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Jack_Buck" title="Jack Buck">Jack<br />Buck</a><br />Broadcaster<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Honored <span style="white-space:nowrap">2002</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Notes:</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Hornsby:</b>  When honored in <a href="/wiki/1937_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1937 St. Louis Cardinals season">1937</a>, \'"SL"\' was used in place of a number as he played mostly in an era without numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<ul><li><b>42:</b>  <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>\'s number 42 was retired throughout baseball in 1997.  The Cardinals again retired 42 in <a href="/wiki/2006_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2006 St. Louis Cardinals season">September 2006</a> in honor of Sutter, who was elected to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Fame</a> earlier in the year.</li>\n<li><b>85:</b>  Cardinal stockholders honored Busch with the number 85 on his 85th birthday in <a href="/wiki/1984_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1984 St. Louis Cardinals season">1984</a>.</li></ul>\n<h4><span id="Out_of_circulation.2C_but_not_officially_retired"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Out_of_circulation,_but_not_officially_retired">Out of circulation, but not officially retired</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Out of circulation, but not officially retired">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<ul><li><b>5:</b>  <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>\' (1B, <a href="/wiki/2001_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2001 St. Louis Cardinals season">2001</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">2011</a>) number has not been reissued since he signed with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a> after the 2011 season.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>\n<li><b>51:</b> <a href="/wiki/Willie_McGee" title="Willie McGee">Willie McGee</a>\'s (OF, <a href="/wiki/1982_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1982 St. Louis Cardinals season">1982</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/1990_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1990 St. Louis Cardinals season">1990</a>, <a href="/wiki/1996_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1996 St. Louis Cardinals season">1996</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/1999_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1999 St. Louis Cardinals season">1999</a>; Coach, <a href="/wiki/1996_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="1996 St. Louis Cardinals season">2018</a>\xe2\x80\x93present) number has not been reissued since late in the <a href="/wiki/2001_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2001 St. Louis Cardinals season">2001</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-snyder_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-189">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>57:</b>  <a href="/wiki/Darryl_Kile" title="Darryl Kile">Darryl Kile</a>\'s (P, <a href="/wiki/2000_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2000 St. Louis Cardinals season">2000</a>\xe2\x80\x93<a href="/wiki/2002_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2002 St. Louis Cardinals season">02</a>) number has not been reissued since his death in the middle of the 2002 season.   Along with <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hancock" title="Josh Hancock">Josh Hancock</a>\'s number 32, another active pitcher deceased in the middle of the season, they are honored with small circular logos bearing their initials and numbers on the wall of the Cardinal bullpen.  During the 2014 playoffs, but following the Cardinals\' elimination, rookie and star prospect Oscar Taveras was killed in a car accident. His number 18 was added along with Kile\'s and Hancock\'s in the home bullpen; however, his number was reissued the following season to close friend <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Martinez_(pitcher,_born_1991)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos Martinez (pitcher, born 1991)">Carlos Martinez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RetiredNumbers_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RetiredNumbers-190">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Minor_league_affiliations">Minor league affiliations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span Peniche</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television_coverage">Radio and television coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Radio and television coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_St._Louis_Cardinals_broadcasters" title="List of St. Louis Cardinals broadcasters">List of St. Louis Cardinals broadcasters</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Capable of reaching 21 million listeners in nine states including <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indiana" title="Indiana">Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>, the Cardinals radio network is the second-largest in MLB with 117 affiliate stations.<sup id="cite_ref-Ratings_among_highest_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratings_among_highest-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  In St. Louis, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>-owned <a href="/wiki/KMOX" title="KMOX">KMOX</a> (1120 AM) airs Cardinals games over radio and feeds the rest of the Cardinals network.  <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shannon" title="Mike Shannon">Mike Shannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Rooney_(sportscaster)" title="John Rooney (sportscaster)">John Rooney</a> alternate as <a href="/wiki/Play-by-play" class="mw-redirect" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> announcers, with Chris Hrabe serving as <a href="/wiki/Pre-game_show" title="Pre-game show">pre-game</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-game_show" title="Post-game show">post-game</a> host.  KMOX\'s 50,000-<a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">watt</a> <a href="/wiki/Clear-channel_station" title="Clear-channel station">clear-channel signal</a> covers much of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental United States">continental United States</a> at night.  At one time, owing to the Cardinals\' status as a "regional" franchise, the Cardinals radio network reached almost half of the country.\n</p><p>The 2011 season marked the Cardinals\' return to KMOX following five seasons on <a href="/wiki/KTRS_(AM)" title="KTRS (AM)">KTRS</a> (550 AM), a station which is 50 percent owned by the Cardinals.  With a partnership spanning seven decades, and continuously since 1954, its conclusion was realized after the 2005 season when <a href="/wiki/CBS_Radio" title="CBS Radio">CBS Radio</a> and the Cardinals failed to reach terms on a new rights agreement.  However, frustrated by the underpowered coverage of 5,000-watt KTRS, the Cardinals reached a new deal with KMOX in 2011.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mike_Shannon" title="Mike Shannon">Mike Shannon</a> announced 30 fewer games in 2013, compared to the 15 he took off in 2012, and in previous seasons.  Most of the games will be road games and three-city trips.  He has been announcing Cardinals\' games starting in 1972, making 2013 his 41st year announcing.  He turns 74 in July.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> He has announced Cardinals\' games for more years than anyone except <a href="/wiki/Jack_Buck" title="Jack Buck">Jack Buck</a> (1954\xe2\x80\x9358, 1961\xe2\x80\x932001) who announced for 46 years.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since 2000, Cardinals telecasts have generated the top three in ratings in MLB every season.<sup id="cite_ref-Ratings_among_highest_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratings_among_highest-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Midwest" title="Fox Sports Midwest">Fox Sports Midwest</a> airs all games in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high-definition</a> and is the team\'s exclusive television broadcaster, with the exception of selected <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_Fox" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on Fox">Saturday afternoon games</a> on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> (via its St. Louis affiliate, <a href="/wiki/KTVI" title="KTVI">KTVI</a>) or <i><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ESPN" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball on ESPN">Sunday Night Baseball</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>.  <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Indiana" title="Fox Sports Indiana">Fox Sports Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_South" title="Fox Sports South">Fox Sports South</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Tennessee" title="Fox Sports Tennessee">Fox Sports Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Oklahoma" title="Fox Sports Oklahoma">Fox Sports Oklahoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Southwest" title="Fox Sports Southwest">Fox Sports Southwest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SportSouth" class="mw-redirect" title="SportSouth">SportSouth</a> air Cardinals games for fans living within the Cardinals broadcast territory who do not receive the Fox Sports Midwest channel. During the 2016 season, the Cardinals averaged a 8.54 rating and 104,000 viewers on primetime TV broadcasts in St Louis.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The television commentators lineup includes <a href="/wiki/Dan_McLaughlin" title="Dan McLaughlin">Dan McLaughlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Horton" class="mw-redirect" title="Rick Horton">Rick Horton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Al_Hrabosky" title="Al Hrabosky">Al Hrabosky</a>.  Jimmy "The Cat" Hayes serves as <a href="/wiki/Field_reporter" class="mw-redirect" title="Field reporter">dugout reporter</a> during the game as well as on <i>Cardinals Live</i>, a pre- and post-game show. <i>Cardinals Live</i> is hosted in-studio by Pat Parris along with game analysts and former Cardinals players <a href="/wiki/Jim_Edmonds" title="Jim Edmonds">Jim Edmonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Bennett_(baseball)" title="Gary Bennett (baseball)">Gary Bennett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Duncan" title="Chris Duncan">Chris Duncan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Cardinals Kids</i>, a program aimed at the team\'s younger fans, airs weekly in-season on Fox Sports Midwest. It\'s hosted by former Cardinals pitcher <a href="/wiki/Andy_Benes" title="Andy Benes">Andy Benes</a>, team mascot <a href="/wiki/Fredbird" title="Fredbird">Fredbird</a>, and Busch Stadium Public Address announcer John "The U-Man" Ulett. The 30-minute show began airing in 2003 and presents team news, player profiles, and Cardinals team history in a kid-friendly manner along with games and trivia.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A weekly magazine program, <i>This Week in Cardinal Nation</i>, airs on St. Louis\' <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/KSDK" title="KSDK">KSDK</a>. Cardinals games had been seen on KSDK (and its predecessor, KSD-TV) from 1947 through 1958, 1963 through 1987, and 2007 until 2010. <a href="/wiki/KPLR-TV" title="KPLR-TV">KPLR-TV</a> was the Cardinals\' other over-the-air broadcaster, carrying games from 1959 through 1962 and from 1988 until 2006.\n</p><p>Former Cardinals broadcasters include <a href="/wiki/Jack_Buck" title="Jack Buck">Jack Buck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Caray" title="Harry Caray">Harry Caray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dizzy_Dean" title="Dizzy Dean">Dizzy Dean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Garagiola,_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Joe Garagiola, Sr.">Joe Garagiola, Sr.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jay_Randolph" title="Jay Randolph">Jay Randolph</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joe_Buck" title="Joe Buck">Joe Buck</a>, the son of Jack Buck, was an official member of the Cardinals\' broadcast team from 1991 until 2007. The younger Buck is currently the lead play-by-play caller for <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(United_States)" title="Fox Sports (United States)">Fox Sports</a>\' national <a href="/wiki/Fox_Major_League_Baseball" title="Fox Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fox_NFL" title="Fox NFL">National Football League</a> broadcasts.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_Day_lineups">Opening Day lineups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Opening Day lineups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F;;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F;;">1\n</th>\n<th style="background-color:#C4203B;color:#FFFFFF;-moz-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; -webkit-box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #22205F, inset -2px -2px 0 #22205F; box-shadow: class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2001, the Cardinals and the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> finished the season with identical records of 93\xe2\x80\x9369 and finished tied for first place in the Central Division standings. The <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> wrote they were both awarded a co-championship.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> According to the Cardinals\' website, this was <i>"the first shared championship in major-league history"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> For playoff seeding, the NL Central slot went to Houston and St. Louis was awarded the wild card berth.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1981, the Cardinals finished with the overall best record in the East Division. However, a <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a> in the middle of the season forced the season to be split into two halves. St. Louis finished second in both halves and was thereby deprived of a post-season appearance.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Most sources consider the 1882 Brown Stockings to represent the beginning of the St. Louis Cardinals (if it was not the even earlier 1875 or 1878 clubs) but the St. Louis Cardinals baseball club itself considers its history to have begun in 1892 when the team (still called the St. Louis Browns) joined the National League.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Although the St. Louis Cardinals do not officially recognize their era in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_(19th_century)" title="American Association (19th century)">American Association</a> (AA) as part of their Major League history, <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball#History" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> recognized that incarnation of the AA in 1968, as well as other historic leagues, existing as former Major Leagues.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._Louis_Cardinals&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
